A terrific gay bar in the middle of nowhere but Freeway close. I enjoy the fact that it features both indoor and outdoor patio areas. <rate>5< /rate><pics>None< /pics><Date>1535235174782< /Date>< user_id>
116544393887558182971</user_id>
< review>
Having to use a funding company is not something I wanted to experience, but hurricanes interrupted business and cash flow so badly in summer 2017 that I felt that I had no other choice. And once you get into the situation of paying back money at an exorbitant cost in a very short period of time, you may likely find that you have to get funding again in order to cover the cash flow for the debt service. And if you get funding from one company, then concurrent funding from additional companies will be priced even higher and/or shorter terms.
If you ever use one funding company, you will be bombarded with solicitations from hundreds salesmen (they call themselves "consultants" or "brokers") with a wide variety of email addresses, UIRL's and phone numbers. Many of these brokers claim to be "direct lenders", but most are not, so don't be fooled by expecting that you will get a better deal thinking that a "direct lender" will not cost as much without a broker's commission. It seems as though they are selling pretty much the same program from a few actual funding companies. These funding companies are not banks, they are investors who hope that the unsecured credit that they extend will be paid back, and, hopefully, within the agreed time frame. And if you don't contract with the broker/salesman/funding company that you talked to, it seems that they share your information with many others so you will be solicited by many, many others. Most of these people are very aggressive, so I assume that their commissions must be incredible. If they get your telephone number, they will use every stunt to get past your receptionist, or, if they get your cell phone number you can expect calls and texts many times per week and even in the evenings.
All of them will ask you to fill out an application (and funny how there seems to be only a couple of variations of applications, like they all share the same web page). After the application, proposals are made. Disregard the offers that you get in the mail or email before you fill-out the application, it is only a come-on to get your attention, even if they say "approved" or "pre-approved".
Then, when you negotiate and agree upon a deal verbally and/or in writing, most turned out to be come-ons that were modified or turned down by the "underwriter" on the day that the money was supposed to be sent. I think that they assume that you are over a barrel and have to take whatever you can get at that point.
Having said all that, I have found that Coconut Funding's people are actually much more direct and less B.S. than most of the others. And, most importantly, they honor the deals that they agreed upon.< /review>

We went for an international health certificate for our service dog to travel to Mexico, something we have gone to this Vet for before as he has been our Vet for years.  The form has to be completed accurately and completely and we were forced to come back multiple times taking an entire day for the form to be completed without mistakes ranging from simple typo's to different addresses in different places.  Once "completed", the form had to be taken to the USDA for certification for airline travel. We made the USDA appointment weeks in advance and had to spend a day getting to LAX, the only USDA office available in California.  Unfortunately, after spending an entire day and hundreds of dollars we were just turned away from USDA since the form was signed by the VET in the USDA box.  This is something we didn't check since frankly, we're not Vets.  Worse, the USDA has no appointments left before our trip so they will not see us again, even if the travel form is corrected.  This now impacts the Christmas and New Years plans of three couples, and likely the loss of thousands of dollars in airfare and the need to re-plan the Holidays.  This was an unforced error, the VET signed in the wrong box and no corrections are not allowed. This not only cost us two days ahead of the trip and multiple visits to the VET, it also ruined our holiday plans.  The USDA office told me they have never seen such an obvious error and that any VET should be competent enough to read and complete the form.  This is just unacceptable, and as a long term customer we are devastated and now find we could not trust our animal to this office that is this cavalier even after being coached through the form and made aware of the criticality of accuracy.<//Review>

< Text>
Our dog needed a last-minute vaccination before going on holiday. Called around and Trinity and they said they could see him as a walk-in that day. The wait was not long, about 1/2 hr, and the staff were all very friendly, helpful, and efficient. The 'exam' (required by most vets before giving vaccines) only lasted a couple of minutes but it was free and the Dr stayed to answer a few questions, gave us some helpful health advice, and renewed a prescription saving us a trip to our regular vet. Also, the charges were very reasonable. They even provided prescription meds for about the same price I pay at Walmart. I will take my pet to them again!<//Text>

<Pictures>None</Pictures>< Review>
I have been with Trinity Hospital for almost 2 years now taking care of my two dogs. I started with them merely because they were around the corner from me. Throughout the time, there have been a few incidents of very disappointing experience:
1. There was once a replacement doctor, who was nothing but a JOKE! The visit session went as if he is there to play with the pets and just try to entertain the pet owner and the pet. Answer to any diagnosis question was "maybe yes, maybe no; everything is possible"... I asked not to be seen by that Dr. ever again and gladly I never was, but I still had to pay for a "visit"!

2. On memorial weekend 2017, I used their boarding services. My only dog at the time was on some medication that was prescribed by Dr. K, himself. I put all the daily medications, labeled nice & neat for AM/PM use. Left a note in the bag for medication, and obviously mentioned to the front desk as well. I picked up my pet after a few days, and when returned home, I found the entire medications (as well as treats, etc.) intact in the bag! Obviously, nobody even touched that bag! I called them specifically about the medications and they pretend that they gave the medication out of their inventor; yea sure!! They preferred not to use the readily available medication that was paid for, and they supplied it on their own cost; yea sure!! They didn't even apologize and acted as if they did their job very much right!

3. On February of 2018, I had one my dogs, who got skin rash and allergy, for a visit, and they gave me a bunch of medications to take home, as if everything all good. It was only me doing the math after a few days, to realize that there is not even enough pills for one of the medications to complete the "treatment period." I called them and they mentioned that yes we were running out of it at the moment. First of all, "running out of medication" is not an excuse to leave treatment period incomplete. Secondly, if that was the case, they should've at least gave me a heads up for the lack of supply, and either offer to supply me later; or at the worse case, I know I have to go supply it from somewhere. Sending a patient home with not enough medicine is very unprofessional and medically wrong.

4. My only reason to go back there after all was ONLY a type of good impression that I had with the main Dr. there (Dr. K), however, a recent disappointing experience took that only remaining motivation away and I am not going back there. My dogs mated in late March/early April, and I had taken them last week for regular vaccination, where they said my female cannot get vaccines while pregnant. Then Dr. K advised on having an X-ray for ONLY reason of being able to count the puppies so after delivery, we could make sure there is nothing stuck in the belly. To my unwillingness of the necessity of doing so (because she was doing great in all aspects), I took that ONLY reason as valid and agreed to the X-ray. The outcome was that Dr. K could only see 6 puppies and his assessment was that she is not due until at least another 3 weeks or so which was strange to me, but I took the word from the expert. To my surprise and my unreadiness, I got caught totally off-guard on Monday, 5/28, to her giving birth to 12 puppies! So not only that X-ray was unuseful (most probably because it was taken not correctly), but it even worked to my disadvantage by not having me properly prepared for the delivery.

5. I called them on Monday morning feeling that my dog could go thru anything during or right after delivery, but their office was completely closed. Then I called them on Tuesday 7 AM describing the (almost emergency) situation and asked to talk to Dr. K. I had a miss call from him on 7:20 PM!! and I ended up talking to him on Wednesday. Even after all the wrong diagnosis and everything else around this unnecessary, unuseful X-Ray and the harms, they even didn't consider a customer courtesy on the service.

and other issues such as rude and unfriendly staff, lack of space for pets and pet owners, etc. are even too minor to mention.<//Review>
